      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Isoroku_Yamamoto&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Personal life">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <table class="metadata plainlinks ambox mbox-small-left ambox-content" role="presentation">
      <tr>
       <td class="mbox-image">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg">
         <img alt="[icon]" data-file-height="31" data-file-width="44" height="14" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/20px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/30px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/40px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png 2x" width="20"/>
        </a>
       </td>
       <td class="mbox-text">
        <span class="mbox-text-span">
         This section requires
         <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Isoroku_Yamamoto&amp;action=edit">
          expansion
         </a>
         .
         <small>
          <i>
           (June 2008)
          </i>
         </small>
        </span>
       </td>
      </tr>
     </table>
     <p>
      While other military leaders avoided the image of being "soft", Yamamoto continued to practice
      <a href="/wiki/Calligraphy" title="Calligraphy">
       calligraphy
      </a>
      . He and his wife, Reiko, had four children: two sons and two daughters. Yamamoto was an avid gambler, enjoying
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Shogi" title="Shogi">
        shogi
       </a>
      </i>
      ,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Billiards" title="Billiards">
       billiards
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Contract_bridge" title="Contract bridge">
       bridge
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mah_jong" title="Mah jong">
       mah jong
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Poker" title="Poker">
       poker
      </a>
      , and other games that tested his wits and sharpened his mind. He frequently made jokes about moving to
      <a href="/wiki/Monaco" title="Monaco">
       Monaco
      </a>
      and starting his own
      <a href="/wiki/Casino" title="Casino">
       casino
      </a>
      . He enjoyed the company of
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Geisha" title="Geisha">
        geisha
       </a>
      </i>
      , and his wife Reiko revealed to the Japanese public in 1954 that Yamamoto was closer to his favorite
      <i>
       geisha
      </i>
      Kawai Chiyoko than to her, which stirred some controversy.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29">
       <a href="#cite_note-29">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        29
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      After his death, his funeral procession passed by Kawai's quarters on the way to the cemetery.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30">
       <a href="#cite_note-30">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        30
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>

     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Yamamoto.27s_career_promotions">
       Yamamoto's career promotions
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Isoroku_Yamamoto&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Yamamoto's career promotions">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <ul>
      <li>
       MidshipmanNovember 14, 1904
      </li>
      <li>
       EnsignAugust 31, 1905
      </li>
      <li>
       SublieutenantSeptember 28, 1907
      </li>
      <li>
       LieutenantOctober 11, 1909
      </li>
      <li>
       Lieutenant CommanderDecember 13, 1915
      </li>
      <li>
       CommanderDecember 1, 1919
      </li>
      <li>
       CaptainDecember 1, 1923
      </li>
      <li>
       Rear AdmiralNovember 30, 1929
      </li>
      <li>
       Vice AdmiralNovember 15, 1934
      </li>
      <li>
       AdmiralNovember 15, 1940
      </li>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Gensui_(Imperial_Japanese_Navy)" title="Gensui (Imperial Japanese Navy)">
        Marshal-Admiral
       </a>
       April 18, 1943 (posthumous)
      </li>
     </ul>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Media_portrayals">
       Media portrayals
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Isoroku_Yamamoto&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Media portrayals">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <p>
      Since the end of the Second World War, a number of Japanese and American films have depicted the character of Isoroku Yamamoto.
     </p>
     <p>
      One of the most notable films is the 1970 movie
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Tora!_Tora!_Tora!" title="Tora! Tora! Tora!">
        Tora! Tora! Tora!
       </a>
      </i>
      , which stars Japanese actor
      <a href="/wiki/So_Yamamura" title="So Yamamura">
       S Yamamura
      </a>
      as Yamamoto, who states after the attack on Pearl Harbor:
     </p>
     <blockquote class="templatequote">
      <p>
       I fear that all we have done is to awaken a sleeping giant and fill him with a terrible resolve.
      </p>
      <div class="templatequotecite">
       
       <a href="/wiki/Isoroku_Yamamoto%27s_sleeping_giant_quote" title="Isoroku Yamamoto's sleeping giant quote">
        attributed to Yamamoto
       </a>
       in
       <i>
        Tora! Tora! Tora!
       </i>
       (1970), in reference to the attack on Pearl Harbor.
      </div>
     </blockquote>
     <p>
      There is no evidence that Yamamoto said this in reality despite the film calling it a quote. (See
      <a href="/wiki/Isoroku_Yamamoto%27s_sleeping_giant_quote" title="Isoroku Yamamoto's sleeping giant quote">
       Isoroku Yamamoto's sleeping giant quote
      </a>
      for further discussion.)
     </p>
     <p>
      The first film to feature Yamamoto was
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Toho_Company" title="Toho Company">
       Toho
      </a>
      's 1953 film
      <i>
       <a class="extiw" href="//ja.wikipedia.org/wiki/%E5%A4%AA%E5%B9%B3%E6%B4%8B%E3%81%AE%E9%B7%B2" title="jp:">
        Taiheiy no washi
       </a>
      </i>
      , (later released in the United States as
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Eagle_of_the_Pacific" title="Eagle of the Pacific">
        Eagle of the Pacific
       </a>
      </i>
      ), in which Yamamoto was portrayed by
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Denjir%C3%B4_%C3%94k%C3%B4chi" title="Denjir kchi">
       Denjir kchi
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31">
       <a href="#cite_note-31">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        31
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The 1960 film
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/The_Gallant_Hours" title="The Gallant Hours">
        The Gallant Hours
       </a>
      </i>
      depicts the battle of wits between Vice-Admiral
      <a href="/wiki/William_Halsey,_Jr." title="William Halsey, Jr.">
       William Halsey, Jr.
      </a>
      and Yamamoto from the start of the
      <a href="/wiki/Guadalcanal_Campaign" title="Guadalcanal Campaign">
       Guadalcanal Campaign
      </a>
      in August 1942 to
      <a href="/wiki/Operation_Vengeance" title="Operation Vengeance">
       Yamamoto's death
      </a>
      in April 1943. The film, however, portrays Yamamoto's death as occurring in November 1942, the day after the Naval Battle of Guadalcanal, and the P-38 aircraft that killed him as coming from Guadalcanal.
     </p>
     <p>
      In
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Daiei_Studios" title="Daiei Studios">
       Daiei Studios
      </a>
      's 1969 film
      <i>
       Aa, kaigun
      </i>
      (later released in the United States as
      <i>
       Gateway to Glory
      </i>
      ), Yamamoto was portrayed by
      <a href="/wiki/Sh%C5%8Dgo_Shimada_(actor)" title="Shgo Shimada (actor)">
       Shgo Shimada
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32">
       <a href="#cite_note-32">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        32
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33">
       <a href="#cite_note-33">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        33
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Award-winning Japanese actor
      <a href="/wiki/Toshiro_Mifune" title="Toshiro Mifune">
       Toshiro Mifune
      </a>
      (star of
      <i>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Seven_Samurai" title="The Seven Samurai">
        The Seven Samurai
       </a>
      </i>
      ) portrayed Yamamoto in three films:
     </p>
     <ul>
      <li>
       <i>
        <a class="extiw" href="//ja.wikipedia.org/wiki/%E9%80%A3%E5%90%88%E8%89%A6%E9%9A%8A%E5%8F%B8%E4%BB%A4%E9%95%B7%E5%AE%98_%E5%B1%B1%E6%9C%AC%E4%BA%94%E5%8D%81%E5%85%AD" title="jp: ">
         Reng Kantai Shirei Chkan: Yamamoto Isoroku
        </a>
       </i>
       (1968, later released in Canada and the United States as
       <i>
        Admiral Yamamoto
       </i>
       ),
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34">
        <a href="#cite_note-34">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         34
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
      <li>
       <i>
        Gekido no showashi 'Gunbatsu'
       </i>
       (1970, lit. "Turning Point of Showa History: The Militarists"),
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35">
        <a href="#cite_note-35">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         35
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       and
      </li>
      <li>
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Midway_(film)" title="Midway (film)">
         Midway
        </a>
       </i>
       (1976, where all of the Japanese scenes had English dialogue).
      </li>
     </ul>
     <p>
      In
      <a href="/wiki/Sh%C5%ABe_Matsubayashi" title="She Matsubayashi">
       She Matsubayashi
      </a>
      's 1981 film
      <i>
       <a class="extiw" href="//ja.wikipedia.org/wiki/%E9%80%A3%E5%90%88%E8%89%A6%E9%9A%8A_(%E6%98%A0%E7%94%BB)" title="jp: ()">
        Reng kantai
       </a>
      </i>
      (lit. "Combined Fleet", later released in the United States as
      <i>
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=The_Imperial_Navy&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="The Imperial Navy (page does not exist)">
        The Imperial Navy
       </a>
      </i>
      ), Yamamoto was portrayed by
      <a href="/wiki/Keiju_Kobayashi" title="Keiju Kobayashi">
       Keiju Kobayashi
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36">
       <a href="#cite_note-36">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        36
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In the 2001 film
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Pearl_Harbor_(film)" title="Pearl Harbor (film)">
        Pearl Harbor
       </a>
      </i>
      , a
      <a href="/wiki/Jerry_Bruckheimer" title="Jerry Bruckheimer">
       Jerry Bruckheimer
      </a>
      -produced
      <a href="/wiki/Epic_film" title="Epic film">
       epic
      </a>
      , Yamamoto was portrayed by Oscar-nominated Japanese-born American actor
      <a href="/wiki/Mako_Iwamatsu" title="Mako Iwamatsu">
       Mako Iwamatsu
      </a>
      . Like
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Tora!_Tora!_Tora!" title="Tora! Tora! Tora!">
        Tora! Tora! Tora!
       </a>
      </i>
      , this film also features
      <a href="/wiki/Isoroku_Yamamoto%27s_sleeping_giant_quote" title="Isoroku Yamamoto's sleeping giant quote">
       the sleeping giant quote
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      In
      <a href="/wiki/Toei_Company" title="Toei Company">
       Toei
      </a>
      's 2011 war film
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Reng%C5%8D_Kantai_Shirei_Ch%C5%8Dkan:_Yamamoto_Isoroku_(2011_film)" title="Reng Kantai Shirei Chkan: Yamamoto Isoroku (2011 film)">
        Reng Kantai Shirei Chkan: Yamamoto Isoroku
       </a>
      </i>
      , Yamamoto was portrayed by
      <a href="/wiki/K%C5%8Dji_Yakusho" title="Kji Yakusho">
       Kji Yakusho
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37">
       <a href="#cite_note-37">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        37
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Alternate_history">
       Alternate history
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Isoroku_Yamamoto&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Alternate history">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      In the 1993
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/OVA" title="OVA">
       OVA
      </a>
      series
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Konpeki_no_Kantai" title="Konpeki no Kantai">
        Konpeki no Kantai
       </a>
      </i>
      (lit.
      <i>
       Deep Blue Fleet
      </i>
      ), the original timeline proceeds
      <a href="/wiki/Operation_Vengeance" title="Operation Vengeance">
       until Yamamoto's death in April 1943
      </a>
      . However, instead of dying in the crash, Yamamoto blacks out and suddenly wakes up as his younger self, Isoroku Takano, after the
      <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Tsushima" title="Battle of Tsushima">
       Battle of Tsushima
      </a>
      in 1905. His memory from the original timeline intact, Yamamoto uses his knowledge of the future to help Japan become a stronger military power, and eventually launching a
      <i>
       coup d'tat
      </i>
      against
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hideki_T%C5%8Dj%C5%8D" title="Hideki Tj">
       Hideki Tj
      </a>
      's government. In the subsequent
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pacific_war" title="Pacific war">
       Pacific war
      </a>
      , Japan's technologically advanced navy decisively defeats the United States, and grants all of the former European and American colonies in Asia full independence. Later on, Yamamoto convinces Japan to join forces with the United States and Britain to defeat Nazi Germany.
     </p>
     <p>
      In the 2004
      <a href="/wiki/Anime" title="Anime">
       anime
      </a>
      series
      <i>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Zipang_(anime)" title="Zipang (anime)">
        Zipang
       </a>
      </i>
      , Yamamoto (who is voiced by
      <a class="extiw" href="//ja.wikipedia.org/wiki/%E5%A4%96%E6%B3%A2%E5%B1%B1%E6%96%87%E6%98%8E" title="jp:">
       Bunmei Tobayama
      </a>
      ) works to develop the uneasy partnership with the crew of the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/DDG-182_Mirai" title="DDG-182 Mirai">
       JMSDF
       <i>
        Mirai
       </i>
      </a>
      , which has been transported back sixty years through time to the year 1942.
     </p>
     <p>
      In the
      <a href="/wiki/Axis_of_Time" title="Axis of Time">
       Axis of Time
      </a>
      trilogy by author
      <a href="/wiki/John_Birmingham" title="John Birmingham">
       John Birmingham
      </a>
      , which depicts an alternate history of World War II, after a naval task force from the year 2021 is accidentally transported back through time to 1942, Yamamoto assumes a leadership role in the dramatic alteration of Japan's war strategy.
     </p>
     <p>
      In
      <a href="/wiki/Douglas_Niles" title="Douglas Niles">
       Douglas Niles
      </a>
      ' 2007 book
      <i>
       MacArthur's War: A Novel of the Invasion of Japan
      </i>
      (written with
      <a href="/wiki/Michael_Dobson_(author)" title="Michael Dobson (author)">
       Michael Dobson
      </a>
      ), which focuses on General
      <a href="/wiki/Douglas_MacArthur" title="Douglas MacArthur">
       Douglas MacArthur
      </a>
      and an alternate history of the
      <a href="/wiki/Pacific_War" title="Pacific War">
       Pacific War
      </a>
      (following a considerably different outcome of the
      <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Midway" title="Battle of Midway">
       Battle of Midway
      </a>
      ), Yamamoto is portrayed sympathetically, with much of the action in the Japanese government seen through his eyes, though he could not change the major decisions of Japan in World War II.
     </p>
     <p>
      In
      <a href="/wiki/Robert_Conroy" title="Robert Conroy">
       Robert Conroy
      </a>
      's 2011 book
      <i>
       Rising Sun
      </i>
      , Yamamoto directs the IJN to launch a series of attacks on the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/American_West_Coast" title="American West Coast">
       American West Coast
      </a>
      , in the hope that the United States can be convinced to sue for peace and securing Japan's place as a world power; but he cannot escape his lingering fear that the war will ultimately doom Japan.
     </p>
     <p>
      In
      <a href="/wiki/Neal_Stephenson" title="Neal Stephenson">
       Neal Stephenson
      </a>
      's 1999 book
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Cryptonomicon" title="Cryptonomicon">
        Cryptonomicon
       </a>
      </i>
      , Yamamoto's final moments are depicted as him realising that
      <a href="/wiki/Japanese_naval_codes" title="Japanese naval codes">
       Japan's cryptographic codes
      </a>
      have been broken, and that he must inform them, right up until he and his chair hit the tree.
     </p>

     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Sources">
       Sources
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Isoroku_Yamamoto&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Sources">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <ul>
      <li>
       Agawa, Hiroyuki; Bester, John (trans.).
       <i>
        The Reluctant Admiral
       </i>
       . New York: Kodansha, 1979.
       <a class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn" href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/9784770025395">
        ISBN 978-4-7700-2539-5
       </a>
       . A definitive biography of Yamamoto in English. This book explains much of the political structure and events within Japan that lead to the war.
      </li>
      <li>
       Davis, Donald A.
       <i>
        Lightning Strike: The Secret Mission to Kill Admiral Yamamoto and Avenge Pearl Harbor
       </i>
       . New York: St. Martin's Press, 2005.
       <a class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn" href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/9780312309060">
        ISBN 978-0-312-30906-0
       </a>
       .
      </li>
      <li>
       Dull, Paul S.
       <i>
        A Battle History of the Imperial Japanese Navy, 19411945
       </i>
       . Annapolis, Maryland: Naval Institute Press, 1978.
       <a class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn" href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/9780870210976">
        ISBN 978-0-87021-097-6
       </a>
       .
      </li>
      <li>
       Evans, David C. and Mark R. Peattie.
       <i>
        Kaigun: Strategy, Tactics, and Technology in the Imperial Japanese Navy 18871941
       </i>
       . Annapolis, Maryland: Naval Institute Press, 1997.
       <a class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn" href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/9780870211928">
        ISBN 978-0-87021-192-8
       </a>
       .
      </li>
      <li>
       Glines, Carroll V.
       <i>
        Attack on Yamamoto
       </i>
       (1st edition). New York: Crown, 1990.
       <a class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn" href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/9780517577288">
        ISBN 978-0-517-57728-8
       </a>
       . Glines documents both the mission to shoot down Yamamoto and the subsequent controversies with thorough research, including personal interviews with all surviving participants and researchers who examined the crash site.
      </li>
      <li>
       Hoyt, Edwin P.
       <i>
        Yamamoto: The Man Who Planned Pearl Harbor
       </i>
       . New York: McGraw-Hill, 1990.
       <a class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn" href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/9781585744282">
        ISBN 978-1-58574-428-2
       </a>
       .
      </li>
      <li>
       Lundstrom, John B.
       <i>
        The First Team: Pacific Naval Air Combat from Pearl Harbor to Midway
       </i>
       . Annapolis, Maryland: Naval Institute Press, 1984.
       <a class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn" href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/9780870211898">
        ISBN 978-0-87021-189-8
       </a>
       .
      </li>
      <li>
       Miller, Edward S.
       <i>
        War Plan Orange: The U.S. Strategy to Defeat Japan, 18971945
       </i>
       . Annapolis, Maryland: Naval Institute Press, 1991.
       <a class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn" href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/9780870217593">
        ISBN 978-0-87021-759-3
       </a>
       .
      </li>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Mark_Peattie" title="Mark Peattie">
        Peattie
       </a>
       , Mark R.
       <i>
        Sunburst: The Rise of Japanese Naval Air Power, 19091941
       </i>
       . Annapolis, Maryland: Naval Institute Press, 2002.
       <a class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn" href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/9781557504326">
        ISBN 978-1-55750-432-6
       </a>
       .
      </li>
      <li>
       Prados, John.
       <i>
        Combined Fleet Decoded: The Secret History of American Intelligence and the Japanese Navy in World War II
       </i>
       . Annapolis, Maryland: Naval Institute Press, 2001.
       <a class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn" href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/9781557504319">
        ISBN 978-1-55750-431-9
       </a>
       .
      </li>
      <li>
       Prange, Gordon.
       <i>
        At Dawn We Slept
       </i>
       . New York: Penguin Books, 1982.
       <a class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn" href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/9780140064551">
        ISBN 978-0-14-006455-1
       </a>
       .
      </li>
      <li>
       Ugaki, Matome; Chihaya, Masataka (trans.).
       <i>
        Fading Victory: The Diary of Admiral Matome Ugaki, 194145
       </i>
       . Pittsburgh: University of Pittsburgh Press, 1991.
       <a class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn" href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/9780822954620">
        ISBN 978-0-8229-5462-0
       </a>
       . Provides a high-level view of the war from the Japanese side, from the diaries of Yamamoto's Chief of Staff, Admiral
       <a href="/wiki/Matome_Ugaki" title="Matome Ugaki">
        Matome Ugaki
       </a>
       . Provides evidence of the intentions of the imperial military establishment to seize Hawaii and to operate against Britain's
       <a href="/wiki/Royal_Navy" title="Royal Navy">
        Royal Navy
       </a>
       in the Indian Ocean. Translated by Masataka Chihaya, this edition contains extensive clarifying notes from the U.S. editors derived from U.S. military histories.
      </li>
      <li>
       <span class="citation book" id="CITEREFParillo2006">
        Parillo, Mark (2006).
        <a class="external text" href="http://books.google.com/books?id=T0gt_RjeCrgC&amp;pg=PA287" rel="nofollow">
         "The United States in the Pacific"
        </a>
        . In Higham, Robin; Harris, Stephen.
        <a class="external text" href="http://books.google.com/?id=T0gt_RjeCrgC" rel="nofollow">
         <i>
          Why Air Forces Fail: the Anatomy of Defeat
         </i>
        </a>
        . The University Press of Kentucky.
        <a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">
         ISBN
        </a>
        <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-0-8131-2374-5" title="Special:BookSources/978-0-8131-2374-5">
         978-0-8131-2374-5
        </a>
        .
       </span>
       <span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AIsoroku+Yamamoto&amp;rft.atitle=The+United+States+in+the+Pacific&amp;rft.aufirst=Mark&amp;rft.aulast=Parillo&amp;rft.au=Parillo%2C+Mark&amp;rft.btitle=Why+Air+Forces+Fail%3A+the+Anatomy+of+Defeat&amp;rft.date=2006&amp;rft.genre=bookitem&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2F%3Fid%3DT0gt_RjeCrgC&amp;rft.isbn=978-0-8131-2374-5&amp;rft.pub=The+University+Press+of+Kentucky&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook">
        <span style="display:none;">
        </span>
       </span>
      </li>
     </ul>
